And if you know nothing about the topic, you need to get someone who knows something about the topic to review it. I do think the hallucination problem can get better, especially in specialised LLMs trained for specific purposes, the public tools made for “everything” will take longer
[2026-01-05T16:40:22Z] Meghna: I work in a biotech and I dropped biology after class 10th. Everything I learnt has been via googling up research papers over the course of my career. [2026-01-05T20:11:18Z] Abhishek Vats: Q. Y was the term Nikola Tesla used for what we now call X-rays. While Wilhelm Röntgen is officially credited with their discovery in 1895, Tesla was experimenting with this "invisible radiant energy" as early as 1894. ↵ Tesla didn't just stumble upon X-rays; he developed a unique system to produce them that differed from the standard methods of the time. Unlike other scientists who used standard batteries, Tesla used his Tesla Coil to produce high-frequency, high-voltage currents. He designed specialized "single-electrode" vacuum tubes. These were more powerful than the Crookes tubes used by his peers, allowing him to take images from much further away—up to 8 feet. His images were startlingly clear. His most famous Y is an 1896 image of his own foot inside a shoe, which clearly showed the bones as well as the metal nails and eyelets of the footwear. Id Y? ‎<This message was edited>

[2026-01-06T09:09:51Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Q. X is American English slang, generally meaning to "get rid of" someone or something. In the hospitality industry, it is used to indicate that an item is no longer available, traditionally from a food or drinks establishment, or referring to a person or people who are not welcome on the premises. Author Jef Klein theorized that the bar Chumley's in the West Village of Lower Manhattan was the source of this etymology. His book _The History and Stories of the Best Bars of New York_ claims that the insiders in police would call Chumley's bar during Prohibition before making a raid and tell the bartender to “X” his customers, meaning that they should exit out the ___ ______ _____ door, while the police would come to the Pamela Court entrance. Id X.

[2026-01-06T23:47:53Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Runways are usually numbered according to their direction, more precisely called runway magnetic bearing or QFU. ↵ Consider a plane flying toward the runway on final approach in a day without any wind. Divide its magnetic heading by 10, round it to the nearest whole number and you'll usually get the runway number. For example, if the magnetic heading is 345° then 345/10=34,5, so the runway number will be 35 which will be a runway used for landings (and takeoffs) to the north.
[2026-01-06T23:48:33Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Thus assignment + taxiing becomes easier based on routes
